If it's anything else (`self_` in practice),\\n41: /// then the signatures don't have a special `self` argument, and\\n42: /// can, therefore, have a different one introduced.\\n43: ///\\n44: /// If `MySelf` is just `Self`, then the types are only valid inside\\n45: /// a trait or a trait impl, where the trait has associated types\\n46: /// for each of the API types. //! Internal interface for communicating between a `proc_macro` client\\n2: //! (a proc macro crate) and a `proc_macro` server (a compiler front-end).\\n3: //!\\n4: //! Serialization (with C ABI buffers) and unique integer handles are employed\\n5: //! to allow safely interfacing between two copies of `proc_macro` built\\n6: //! (from the same source) by different compilers with potentially mismatching\\n7: //! Rust ABIs (e.g., stage0/bin/rustc vs stage1/bin/rustc during bootstrap).\\n8: \\n9: #![deny(unsafe_code)]\\n10: \\n11: use std::hash::Hash;\\n12: use std::ops::{Bound, Range};\\n13: use std::sync::Once;\\n14: use std::{fmt, marker, mem, panic, thread};\\n15: \\n16: use crate::{Delimiter, Level, Spacing};\\n17: \\n18: /// Higher-order macro describing the server RPC API, allowing automatic\\n19: /// generation of type-safe Rust APIs, both client-side and server-side.\\n20: ///\\n21: /// `with_api!(MySelf, my_self, my_macro)` expands to:\\n22: /// ```rust,ignore (pseudo-code)\\n23: /// my_macro! {\\n24: ///     // ...\\n25: ///     Literal {\\n26: ///         // ...\\n27: ///         fn character(ch: char) -> MySelf::Literal;\\n28: ///         // ...\\n29: ///         fn span(my_self: &MySelf::Literal) -> MySelf::Span;\\n30: ///         fn set_span(my_self: &mut MySelf::Literal, span: MySelf::Span);\\n31: ///     },\\n32: ///     // ...\\n33: /// }\\n34: /// ```\\n35: ///\\n36: /// The first two arguments serve to customize the arguments names\\n37: /// and argument/return types, to enable several different usecases:\\n38: ///\\n39: /// If `my_self` is just `self`, then each `fn` signature can be used\\n40: /// as-is for a method. If it's anything else (`self_` in practice),\\n41: /// then the signatures don't have a special `self` argument, and\\n42: /// can, therefore, have a different one introduced.\\n43: ///\\n44: /// If `MySelf` is just `Self`, then the types are only valid inside\\n45: /// a trait or a trait impl, where the trait has associated types\\n46: /// for each of the API types. //! Internal interface for communicating between a `proc_macro` client\n2: //! (a proc macro crate) and a `proc_macro` server (a compiler front-end).\n3: //!\n4: //! Serialization (with C ABI buffers) and unique integer handles are employed\n5: //! to allow safely interfacing between two copies of `proc_macro` built\n6: //! (from the same source) by different compilers with potentially mismatching\n7: //! Rust ABIs (e.g., stage0/bin/rustc vs stage1/bin/rustc during bootstrap).\n8: \n9: #![deny(unsafe_code)]\n10: \n11: use std::hash::Hash;\n12: use std::ops::{Bound, Range};\n13: use std::sync::Once;\n14: use std::{fmt, marker, mem, panic, thread};\n15: \n16: use crate::{Delimiter, Level, Spacing};\n17: \n18: /// Higher-order macro describing the server RPC API, allowing automatic\n19: /// generation of type-safe Rust APIs, both client-side and server-side.\n20: ///\n21: /// `with_api!(MySelf, my_self, my_macro)` expands to:\n22: /// ```rust,ignore (pseudo-code)\n23: /// my_macro! {\n24: ///     // ...\n25: ///     Literal {\n26: ///         // ...\n27: ///         fn character(ch: char) -> MySelf::Literal;\n28: ///         // ...\n29: ///         fn span(my_self: &MySelf::Literal) -> MySelf::Span;\n30: ///         fn set_span(my_self: &mut MySelf::Literal, span: MySelf::Span);\n31: ///     },\n32: ///     // ...\n33: /// }\n34: /// ```\n35: ///\n36: /// The first two arguments serve to customize the arguments names\n37: /// and argument/return types, to enable several different usecases:\n38: ///\n39: /// If `my_self` is just `self`, then each `fn` signature can be used\n40: /// as-is for a method. If it's anything else (`self_` in practice),\n41: /// then the signatures don't have a special `self` argument, and\n42: /// can, therefore, have a different one introduced.\n43: ///\n44: /// If `MySelf` is just `Self`, then the types are only valid inside\n45: /// a trait or a trait impl, where the trait has associated types\n46: /// for each of the API types. If non-associated types are desired,\n47: /// a module name (`self` in practice) can be used instead of `Self`.\n48: macro_rules! with_api {\n49:     ($S:ident, $self:ident, $m:ident) => {\n50:         $m! {\n51:             FreeFunctions {\n52:                 fn drop($self: $S::FreeFunctions);\n53:                 fn injected_env_var(var: &str) -> Option<String>;\n54:                 fn track_env_var(var: &str, value: Option<&str>);\n55:                 fn track_path(path: &str);\n56:                 fn literal_from_str(s: &str) -> Result<Literal<$S::Span, $S::Symbol>, ()>;\n57:                 fn emit_diagnostic(diagnostic: Diagnostic<$S::Span>);\n58:             },\n59:             TokenStream {\n60:                 fn drop($self: $S::TokenStream);\n61:                 fn clone($self: &$S::TokenStream) -> $S::TokenStream;\n62:                 fn is_empty($self: &$S::TokenStream) -> bool;\n63:                 fn expand_expr($self: &$S::TokenStream) -> Result<$S::TokenStream, ()>;\n64:                 fn from_str(src: &str) -> $S::TokenStream;\n65:                 fn to_string($self: &$S::TokenStream) -> String;\n66:                 fn from_token_tree(\n67:                     tree: TokenTree<$S::TokenStream, $S::Span, $S::Symbol>,\n68:                 ) -> $S::TokenStream;\n69:                 fn concat_trees(\n70:                     base: Option<$S::TokenStream>,\n71:                     trees: Vec<TokenTree<$S::TokenStream, $S::Span, $S::Symbol>>,\n72:                 ) -> $S::TokenStream;\n73:                 fn concat_streams(\n74:                     base: Option<$S::TokenStream>,\n75:                     streams: Vec<$S::TokenStream>,\n76:                 ) -> $S::TokenStream;\n77:                 fn into_trees(\n78:                     $self: $S::TokenStream\n79:                 ) -> Vec<TokenTree<$S::TokenStream, $S::Span, $S::Symbol>>;\n80:             },\n81:             Span {\n82:                 fn debug($self: $S::Span) -> String;\n83:                 fn parent($self: $S::Span) -> Option<$S::Span>;\n84:                 fn source($self: $S::Span) -> $S::Span;\n85:                 fn byte_range($self: $S::Span) -> Range<usize>;\n86:                 fn start($self: $S::Span) -> $S::Span;\n87:                 fn end($self: $S::Span) -> $S::Span;\n88:                 fn line($self: $S::Span) -> usize;\n89:                 fn column($self: $S::Span) -> usize;\n90:                 fn file($self: $S::Span) -> String;\n91:                 fn local_file($self: $S::Span) -> normalize_and_validate_ident(string: &str) -> Result<$S::Symbol, ()>;\n101:             },\n102:         }\n103:     };\n104: }\n105: \n106: // Similar to `with_api`, but only lists the types Organization. The compiler is a _huge_ codebase; it would be an impossibly\n111:    large crate. In part, the dependency structure reflects the code structure\n112:    of the compiler.\n113: 2. In\n115:    particular, we try to have as few dependencies between crates as possible so\n116:    that we don't have to rebuild as many crates if you change one.\n117: ","endLine":117,"startLine":107},{"content":"66: 1. `rustc` (the binary) calls [`rustc_driver::main`][main].\n67: 1. It is a\n70:    fairly generic interface for driving the whole compilation.\n71: 1. Most of the other `rustc_*` crates depend on [`rustc_middle`], which defines\n72:    a lot of central data structures in the compiler.\n73: 1. The query system is defined\n127: in [`rustc_middle`], so nearly all subsequent parts of the compiler depend on\n128: this crate. It is a really large crate, leading to long compile times.
